206	a pip requirements file on the local filesystem (e.g. ``"requirements.txt"``). If provided, this
207	describes additional pip requirements that are appended to a default set of pip requirements
208	generated automatically based on the user's current software environment. Both requirements and
209	constraints are automatically parsed and written to ``requirements.txt`` and ``constraints.txt``
210	files, respectively, and stored as part of the model. Requirements are also written to the ``pip``
211	section of the model's conda environment (``conda.yaml``) file.
212	
213	.. warning::
214	    The following arguments can't be specified at the same time:

217	    - ``pip_requirements``
218	    - ``extra_pip_requirements``

220	`This example <https://github.com/mlflow/mlflow/blob/master/examples/pip_requirements/pip_requirements.py>`_ demonstrates how to specify pip requirements using
221	``pip_requirements`` and ``extra_pip_requirements``."""  # noqa: E501
222	        ),
223	        "signature": (
224	            """an instance of the :py:class:`ModelSignature <mlflow.models.ModelSignature>`
225	class that describes the model's inputs and outputs. If not specified but an
226	``input_example`` is supplied, a signature will be automatically inferred
227	based on the supplied input example and model. To disable automatic signature
228	inference when providing an input example, set ``signature`` to ``False``.
229	To manually infer a model signature, call
230	:py:func:`infer_signature() <mlflow.models.infer_signature>` on datasets
231	with valid model inputs, such as a training dataset with the target column
232	omitted, and valid model outputs, like model predictions made on the training
233	dataset, for example:
234	
235	.. code-block:: python
236	
237	    from mlflow.models import infer_signature
238	
239	    train = df.drop_column("target_label")
240	    predictions = ...  # compute model predictions
241	    signature = infer_signature(train, predictions)
242	"""

244	        "metadata": (
245	            "Custom metadata dictionary passed to the model and stored in the MLmodel file."
246	        ),
247	        "input_example": (
248	            """one or several instances of valid model input. The input example is used
249	as a hint of what data to feed the model. It will be converted to a Pandas
250	DataFrame and then serialized to json using the Pandas split-oriented
251	format, or a numpy array where the example will be serialized to json
252	by converting it to a list. Bytes are base64-encoded. When the ``signature`` parameter is
253	``None``, the input example is used to infer a model signature.
254	"""
255	        ),
256	        "example_no_conversion": (

258	It's no longer used and can be safely removed. Input examples are not converted anymore.
259	"""

261	        "prompt_template": (
262	            """A string that, if provided, will be used to format the user's input prior
263	to inference. The string should contain a single placeholder, ``{prompt}``, which will be
264	replaced with the user's input. For example: ``"Answer the following question. Q: {prompt} A:"``.
265	
266	Currently, only the following pipeline types are supported:
267

270	- `summarization <https://huggingface.co/transformers/main_classes/pipelines.html#transformers.SummarizationPipeline>`_
271	- `text2text-generation <https://huggingface.co/transformers/main_classes/pipelines.html#transformers.Text2TextGenerationPipeline>`_

278	is loaded. Files declared as dependencies for a given model should have relative
279	imports declared from a common root path if multiple files are defined with import dependencies
280	between them to avoid import errors when loading the model.
281	
282	For a detailed explanation of ``code_paths`` functionality, recommended usage patterns and
283	limitations, see the
284	`code_paths usage guide <https://mlflow.org/docs/latest/model/dependencies.html?highlight=code_paths#saving-extra-code-with-an-mlflow-model>`_.
285	"""
286	        ),
287	        # Only pyfunc flavor supports `infer_code_paths`.
288	        "code_paths_pyfunc": (
289	            """A list of local filesystem paths to Python file dependencies (or directories
290	containing file dependencies). These files are *prepended* to the system path when the model
291	is loaded. Files declared as dependencies for a given model should have relative
292	imports declared from a common root path if multiple files are defined with import dependencies
293	between them to avoid import errors when loading the model.
294	
295	You can leave ``code_paths`` argument unset but set ``infer_code_paths`` to ``True`` to let MLflow
296	infer the model code paths. See ``infer_code_paths`` argument doc for details.
297	
298	For a detailed explanation of ``code_paths`` functionality, recommended usage patterns and
299	limitations, see the
300	`code_paths usage guide <https://mlflow.org/docs/latest/model/dependencies.html?highlight=code_paths#saving-extra-code-with-an-mlflow-model>`_.
301	"""
302	        ),
303	        "infer_code_paths": (
304	            """If set to ``True``, MLflow automatically infers model code paths. The inferred
305	            code path files only include necessary python module files. Only python code files
306	            under current working directory are automatically inferable. Default value is
307	            ``False``.
308	
309	.. warning::
310	    Please ensure that the custom python module code does not contain sensitive data such as
311	    credential token strings, otherwise they might be included in the automatic inferred code
312	    path files and be logged to MLflow artifact repository.
313	
314	    If your custom python module depends on non-python files (e.g. a JSON file) with a relative
315	    path to the module code file path, the non-python files can't be automatically inferred as the
316	    code path file. To address this issue, you should put all used non-python files outside
317	    your custom code directory.
318	
319	    If a python code file is loaded as the python ``__main__`` module, then this code file can't be
320	    inferred as the code path file. If your model depends on classes / functions defined in
321	    ``__main__`` module, you should use `cloudpickle` to dump your model instance in order to pickle
322	    classes / functions in ``__main__``.
323	
324	.. Note:: Experimental: This parameter may change or be removed in a future release without warning.
325	"""
326	        ),
327	        "save_pretrained": (
328	            """If set to ``False``, MLflow will not save the Transformer model weight files,
329	instead only saving the reference to the HuggingFace Hub model repository and its commit hash.
330	This is useful when you load the pretrained model from HuggingFace Hub and want to log or save
331	it to MLflow without modifying the model weights. In such case, specifying this flag to
332	``False`` will save the storage space and reduce time to save the model. Please refer to the
333	`Storage-Efficient Model Logging
334	<../../llms/transformers/large-models.html#transformers-save-pretrained-guide>`_ for more detailed
335	usage.
336	
337	
338	.. warning::
339	
340	    If the model is saved with ``save_pretrained`` set to ``False``, the model cannot be
341	    registered to the MLflow Model Registry. In order to convert the model to the one that
342	    can be registered, you can use :py:func:`mlflow.transformers.persist_pretrained_model()`
343	    to download the model weights from the HuggingFace Hub and save it in the existing model
344	    artifacts. Please refer to `Transformers flavor documentation
345	    <../../llms/transformers/large-models.html#persist-pretrained-guide>`_
346	    for more detailed usage.
347	
348	    .. code-block:: python
349	
350	        import mlflow.transformers
351	
352	        model_uri = "YOUR_MODEL_URI_LOGGED_WITH_SAVE_PRETRAINED_FALSE"
353	        model = mlflow.transformers.persist_pretrained_model(model_uri)
354	        mlflow.register_model(model_uri, "model_name")
355	
356	.. important::
357	
358	    When you save the `PEFT <https://huggingface.co/docs/peft/en/index>`_ model, MLflow will
359	    override the `save_pretrained` flag to `False` and only store the PEFT adapter weights. The
360	    base model weights are not saved but the reference to the HuggingFace repository and
361	    its commit hash are logged instead.
362	"""
363	        ),
364	        "auth_policy": (
365	            """Specifies the authentication policy for the model, which includes two key components.
366	            Note that only one of `auth_policy` or `resources` should be defined.
367	
368	                - **System Auth Policy**: A list of resources required to serve this model.
369	                - **User Auth Policy**: A minimal list of scopes that the user should have access to
370	                    ,in order to invoke this model.
371	
372	    .. Note::
373	        Experimental: This parameter may change or be removed in a future release without warning.
374	            """
375	        ),
376	        "params": "A dictionary of parameters to log with the model.",
377	        "tags": "A dictionary of tags to log with the model.",
378	        "model_type": "The type of the model.",
379	        "step": "The step at which to log the model outputs and metrics",
380	        "model_id": "The ID of the model.",
381	        "prompts": """\
382	A list of prompt URIs registered in the MLflow Prompt Registry, to be associated with the model.
383	Each prompt URI should be in the form ``prompt:/<name>/<version>``. The prompts should be
384	registered in the MLflow Prompt Registry before being associated with the model.
385	
386	This will create a mutual link between the model and the prompt. The associated prompts can be
387	seen in the model's metadata stored in the MLmodel file. From the Prompt Registry UI, you can
388	navigate to the model as well.
389	
390	.. code-block:: python
391	
392	    import mlflow
393	
394	    prompt_template = "Hi, {name}! How are you doing today?"
395	
396	    # Register a prompt in the MLflow Prompt Registry
397	    mlflow.prompts.register_prompt("my_prompt", prompt_template, description="A simple prompt")
398	
399	    # Log a model with the registered prompt
400	    with mlflow.start_run():
401	        model_info = mlflow.pyfunc.log_model(
402	            MyModel(),
403	            artifact_path="model",
404	            prompts=["prompt:/my_prompt/1"]
405	        )
406	
407	    print(model_info.prompts)
408	    # Output: ['prompt:/my_prompt/1']
409	
410	    # Load the prompt
411	    prompt = mlflow.load_prompt(model_info.prompts[0])
412	""",
413	    }
414	)

417	def get_module_min_and_max_supported_ranges(flavor_name):
418	    """
419	    Extracts the minimum and maximum supported package versions from the provided module name.
420	    The version information is provided via the yaml-to-python-script generation script in
421	    dev/update_ml_package_versions.py which writes a python file to the importable namespace of
422	    mlflow.ml_package_versions
423	
424	    Args:
425	        flavor_name: The flavor name registered in ml_package_versions.py
426	
427	    Returns:
428	        tuple of module name, minimum supported version, maximum supported version as strings.
429	    """
430	    if flavor_name == "pyspark.ml":
431	        # pyspark.ml is a special case of spark flavor
432	        flavor_name = "spark"
433	
434	    module_name = _ML_PACKAGE_VERSIONS[flavor_name]["package_info"].get("module_name", flavor_name)
435	    versions = _ML_PACKAGE_VERSIONS[flavor_name]["models"]
436	    min_version = versions["minimum"]
437	    max_version = versions["maximum"]
438	    return module_name, min_version, max_version
439	
440	
441	def _do_version_compatibility_warning(msg: str):
442	    """
443	    Isolate the warn call to show the warning only once.
444	    """
445	    warnings.warn(msg, category=UserWarning, stacklevel=2)
446	
447	
448	def docstring_version_compatibility_warning(integration_name):
449	    """
450	    Generates a docstring that can be applied as a note stating a version compatibility range for
451	    a given flavor and optionally raises a warning if the installed version is outside of the
452	    supported range.
453	
454	    Args:
455	        integration_name: The name of the module as stored within ml-package-versions.yml
456	
457	    Returns:
458	        The wrapped function with the additional docstring header applied
459	    """
460	
461	    def annotated_func(func):
462	        # NB: if using this decorator, ensure the package name to module name reference is
463	        # updated with the flavor's `save` and `load` functions being used within
464	        # ml-package-version.yml file.
465	        min_ver, max_ver, pip_release = get_min_max_version_and_pip_release(
466	            integration_name, "models"
467	        )
468	        notice = (
469	            f"The '{integration_name}' MLflow Models integration is known to be compatible with "
470	            f"``{min_ver}`` <= ``{pip_release}`` <= ``{max_ver}``. "
471	            f"MLflow Models integrations with {integration_name} may not succeed when used with "
472	            "package versions outside of this range."
473	        )
474	
475	        func.__doc__ = (
476	            "    .. Note:: " + notice + "\n" * 2 + func.__doc__ if func.__doc__ else notice
477	        )
478	
479	        return func

   More Info: https://bandit.readthedocs.io/en/latest/plugins/b824_url_found.html
288	        "code_paths_pyfunc": (
289	            """A list of local filesystem paths to Python file dependencies (or directories
290	containing file dependencies). These files are *prepended* to the system path when the model
291	is loaded. Files declared as dependencies for a given model should have relative
292	imports declared from a common root path if multiple files are defined with import dependencies
293	between them to avoid import errors when loading the model.
294	
295	You can leave ``code_paths`` argument unset but set ``infer_code_paths`` to ``True`` to let MLflow
296	infer the model code paths. See ``infer_code_paths`` argument doc for details.
297	
298	For a detailed explanation of ``code_paths`` functionality, recommended usage patterns and
299	limitations, see the
300	`code_paths usage guide <https://mlflow.org/docs/latest/model/dependencies.html?highlight=code_paths#saving-extra-code-with-an-mlflow-model>`_.
301	"""
302	        ),
303	        "infer_code_paths": (
304	            """If set to ``True``, MLflow automatically infers model code paths. The inferred
305	            code path files only include necessary python module files. Only python code files
306	            under current working directory are automatically inferable. Default value is
307	            ``False``.
308	
309	.. warning::
310	    Please ensure that the custom python module code does not contain sensitive data such as
311	    credential token strings, otherwise they might be included in the automatic inferred code
312	    path files and be logged to MLflow artifact repository.
313	
314	    If your custom python module depends on non-python files (e.g. a JSON file) with a relative
315	    path to the module code file path, the non-python files can't be automatically inferred as the
316	    code path file. To address this issue, you should put all used non-python files outside
317	    your custom code directory.
318	
319	    If a python code file is loaded as the python ``__main__`` module, then this code file can't be
320	    inferred as the code path file. If your model depends on classes / functions defined in
321	    ``__main__`` module, you should use `cloudpickle` to dump your model instance in order to pickle
322	    classes / functions in ``__main__``.
323	
324	.. Note:: Experimental: This parameter may change or be removed in a future release without warning.
325	"""
326	        ),
327	        "save_pretrained": (
328	            """If set to ``False``, MLflow will not save the Transformer model weight files,
329	instead only saving the reference to the HuggingFace Hub model repository and its commit hash.
330	This is useful when you load the pretrained model from HuggingFace Hub and want to log or save
331	it to MLflow without modifying the model weights. In such case, specifying this flag to
332	``False`` will save the storage space and reduce time to save the model. Please refer to the
333	`Storage-Efficient Model Logging
334	<../../llms/transformers/large-models.html#transformers-save-pretrained-guide>`_ for more detailed
335	usage.
336	
337	
338	.. warning::
339	
340	    If the model is saved with ``save_pretrained`` set to ``False``, the model cannot be
341	    registered to the MLflow Model Registry. In order to convert the model to the one that
342	    can be registered, you can use :py:func:`mlflow.transformers.persist_pretrained_model()`
343	    to download the model weights from the HuggingFace Hub and save it in the existing model
344	    artifacts. Please refer to `Transformers flavor documentation
345	    <../../llms/transformers/large-models.html#persist-pretrained-guide>`_
346	    for more detailed usage.
347	
348	    .. code-block:: python
349	
350	        import mlflow.transformers
351	
352	        model_uri = "YOUR_MODEL_URI_LOGGED_WITH_SAVE_PRETRAINED_FALSE"
353	        model = mlflow.transformers.persist_pretrained_model(model_uri)
354	        mlflow.register_model(model_uri, "model_name")
355	
356	.. important::
357	
358	    When you save the `PEFT <https://huggingface.co/docs/peft/en/index>`_ model, MLflow will
359	    override the `save_pretrained` flag to `False` and only store the PEFT adapter weights. The
360	    base model weights are not saved but the reference to the HuggingFace repository and
361	    its commit hash are logged instead.
362	"""
363	        ),
364	        "auth_policy": (
365	            """Specifies the authentication policy for the model, which includes two key components.
366	            Note that only one of `auth_policy` or `resources` should be defined.
367	
368	                - **System Auth Policy**: A list of resources required to serve this model.
369	                - **User Auth Policy**: A minimal list of scopes that the user should have access to
370	                    ,in order to invoke this model.
371	
372	    .. Note::
373	        Experimental: This parameter may change or be removed in a future release without warning.
374	            """
375	        ),
376	        "params": "A dictionary of parameters to log with the model.",
377	        "tags": "A dictionary of tags to log with the model.",
378	        "model_type": "The type of the model.",
379	        "step": "The step at which to log the model outputs and metrics",
380	        "model_id": "The ID of the model.",
381	        "prompts": """\
382	A list of prompt URIs registered in the MLflow Prompt Registry, to be associated with the model.
383	Each prompt URI should be in the form ``prompt:/<name>/<version>``. The prompts should be
384	registered in the MLflow Prompt Registry before being associated with the model.
385	
386	This will create a mutual link between the model and the prompt. The associated prompts can be
387	seen in the model's metadata stored in the MLmodel file. From the Prompt Registry UI, you can
388	navigate to the model as well.
389	
390	.. code-block:: python
391	
392	    import mlflow
393	
394	    prompt_template = "Hi, {name}! How are you doing today?"
395	
396	    # Register a prompt in the MLflow Prompt Registry
397	    mlflow.prompts.register_prompt("my_prompt", prompt_template, description="A simple prompt")
398	
399	    # Log a model with the registered prompt
400	    with mlflow.start_run():
401	        model_info = mlflow.pyfunc.log_model(
402	            MyModel(),
403	            artifact_path="model",
404	            prompts=["prompt:/my_prompt/1"]
405	        )
406	
407	    print(model_info.prompts)
408	    # Output: ['prompt:/my_prompt/1']
409	
410	    # Load the prompt
411	    prompt = mlflow.load_prompt(model_info.prompts[0])
412	""",
413	    }
414	)

416	
417	def get_module_min_and_max_supported_ranges(flavor_name):
418	    """
419	    Extracts the minimum and maximum supported package versions from the provided module name.
420	    The version information is provided via the yaml-to-python-script generation script in
421	    dev/update_ml_package_versions.py which writes a python file to the importable namespace of
422	    mlflow.ml_package_versions
423	
424	    Args:
425	        flavor_name: The flavor name registered in ml_package_versions.py
426	
427	    Returns:
428	        tuple of module name, minimum supported version, maximum supported version as strings.
429	    """
430	    if flavor_name == "pyspark.ml":
431	        # pyspark.ml is a special case of spark flavor
432	        flavor_name = "spark"
433	
434	    module_name = _ML_PACKAGE_VERSIONS[flavor_name]["package_info"].get("module_name", flavor_name)
435	    versions = _ML_PACKAGE_VERSIONS[flavor_name]["models"]
436	    min_version = versions["minimum"]
437	    max_version = versions["maximum"]
438	    return module_name, min_version, max_version
439	
440	
441	def _do_version_compatibility_warning(msg: str):
442	    """
443	    Isolate the warn call to show the warning only once.
444	    """
445	    warnings.warn(msg, category=UserWarning, stacklevel=2)
446	
447	
448	def docstring_version_compatibility_warning(integration_name):
449	    """
450	    Generates a docstring that can be applied as a note stating a version compatibility range for
451	    a given flavor and optionally raises a warning if the installed version is outside of the
452	    supported range.
453	
454	    Args:
455	        integration_name: The name of the module as stored within ml-package-versions.yml
456	
457	    Returns:
458	        The wrapped function with the additional docstring header applied
459	    """
460	
461	    def annotated_func(func):
462	        # NB: if using this decorator, ensure the package name to module name reference is
463	        # updated with the flavor's `save` and `load` functions being used within
464	        # ml-package-version.yml file.
465	        min_ver, max_ver, pip_release = get_min_max_version_and_pip_release(
466	            integration_name, "models"
467	        )
468	        notice = (
469	            f"The '{integration_name}' MLflow Models integration is known to be compatible with "
470	            f"``{min_ver}`` <= ``{pip_release}`` <= ``{max_ver}``. "
471	            f"MLflow Models integrations with {integration_name} may not succeed when used with "
472	            "package versions outside of this range."
473	        )
474	
475	        func.__doc__ = (
476	            "    .. Note:: " + notice + "\n" * 2 + func.__doc__ if func.__doc__ else notice
477	        )
478	
479	        return func
480	
481	    return annotated_func
